</p><p>In addition to his tomb, Shen Kuo's <i>Mengxi</i> garden estate, his former two-acre (8,000 m<sup>2</sup>) property in Zhenjiang, was restored by the government in 1985.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Talking_Park_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-Talking_Park-172">[167]</a></sup> However, the renovated Mengxi Garden is only part of the original of Shen Kuo's time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mengxi_Garden_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mengxi_Garden-173">[168]</a></sup> A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qing_Dynasty" title="Qing Dynasty">Qing Dynasty</a> era hall built on the site is now used as the main admissions gate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Talking_Park_172-1"><a href="#cite_note-Talking_Park-172">[167]</a></sup> In the Memorial Hall of the gardens, there is a large painting depicting the original garden of Shen Kuo's time, including wells, green bamboo groves, stone-paved paths, and decorated walls of the original halls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mengxi_Garden_173-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mengxi_Garden-173">[168]</a></sup> In this exhibition hall there stands a 1.4 m (4.6 ft) tall statue of Shen Kuo sitting on a platform, along with centuries-old published copies of his <i>Dream Pool Essays</i> in glass cabinets, one of which is from Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mengxi_Garden_173-2"><a href="#cite_note-Mengxi_Garden-173">[168]</a></sup> At the garden estate there are also displayed marble banners, statues of Shen Kuo, and a model of an armillary sphere; a small museum gallery depicts Shen's various achievements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Talking_Park_172-2"><a href="#cite_note-Talking_Park-172">[167]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Purple_Mountain_Observatory" title="Purple Mountain Observatory">Purple Mountain Observatory</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nanjing" title="Nanjing">Nanjing</a> discovered a new <a href="/wiki/Asteroid" title="Asteroid">asteroid</a> in 1964 and named it after Shen Kuo (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2027_Shen_Guo" title="2027 Shen Guo">2027 Shen Guo</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[169]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shen_Kuo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

Ann Arbor: University of Michigan Press. <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-89264-800-7" title="Special:BookSources/0-89264-800-7">0-89264-800-7</a></li>
<li>Tao, Jie, Zheng Bijun and Shirley L. Mow. (2004). <i>Holding Up Half the Sky: Chinese Women Past, Present, and Future</i>. New York: Feminist Press. <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1-55861-465-6" title="Special:BookSources/1-55861-465-6">1-55861-465-6</a>.</li>
<li>Wu, Kuang Ch'ing. "Ming Printing and Printers," <i>Harvard Journal of Asiatic Studies</i> (February 1943): 203–260.</li>
<li>Yao, Xinzhong. (2003). <i>RoutledgeCurzon Encyclopedia of Confucianism: Volume 2, O–Z</i>. New York: Routledge. <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-7007-1199-6" title="Special:BookSources/0-7007-1199-6">0-7007-1199-6</a>.</li>
<li>Zhang, Yunming (1986). <i>Isis: The History of Science Society: Ancient Chinese Sulfur Manufacturing Processes</i>. Chicago: University of Chicago Press. According to Sivin (1995), III, 49—historian <a href="/wiki/Nathan_Sivin" title="Nathan Sivin">Nathan Sivin</a>—Zhang's biography on Shen is of great importance as it contains the fullest and most accurate account of Shen Kuo's life.</li></ul>
</div>
